<div id="review_1246095572" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1246095572" />
    <a title="Mary ~Ravager of Tomes~" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1452829-mary-ravager-of-tomes"><img alt="Mary ~Ravager of Tomes~" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1598297811p2/1452829.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1246095572?book_show_action=true">Mar 05, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Mary ~Ravager of Tomes~" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Mary ~Ravager of Tomes~" href="/user/show/1452829-mary-ravager-of-tomes">Mary ~Ravager of Tomes~</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1452829-mary-ravager-of-tomes?shelf=year-2018">year-2018</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1452829-mary-ravager-of-tomes?shelf=2-star">2-star</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1452829-mary-ravager-of-tomes?shelf=audiobook">audiobook</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1246095572" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer17411223366575755099">Uhh... WELL. I don't really know what went wrong with me and this book.<br/><br/>I was supposed to enjoy it.<br/><br/><i>I was supposed to really enjoy it.</i><br/><br/><i>
  <b>I was totally expecting to really enjoy it.</b>
</i><br/><br/>But sadly, I didn't.<br/><br/>I have heard <b>so much praise</b> for author <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/125308.Cinda_Williams_Chima' title='Cinda Williams Chima' rel='nofollow noopener'>Cinda Williams Chima</a>, but for now I'm left wishing I could see what so many others have seen in her books.<br/><br/>I actually had a weird experience where I was under the impression that this series was a <b>completely different story</b> than it turned out to be. I'm sure that</span>
  <span id="freeText17411223366575755099" style="display:none">Uhh... WELL. I don't really know what went wrong with me and this book.<br><br>I was supposed to enjoy it.<br><br><i>I was supposed to really enjoy it.</i><br><br><i>
  <b>I was totally expecting to really enjoy it.</b>
</i><br><br>But sadly, I didn't.<br><br>I have heard <b>so much praise</b> for author <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/125308.Cinda_Williams_Chima" title="Cinda Williams Chima" rel="nofollow noopener">Cinda Williams Chima</a>, but for now I'm left wishing I could see what so many others have seen in her books.<br><br>I actually had a weird experience where I was under the impression that this series was a <b>completely different story</b> than it turned out to be. I'm sure that's the result of reading hundreds of synopses between the first time <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/6342491.The_Demon_King__Seven_Realms___1_" title="The Demon King (Seven Realms, #1) by Cinda Williams Chima" rel="nofollow noopener">The Demon King</a> crossed my radar &amp; the time I finally picked it up. <br><br>Standing at the end of this book, I can't even remember what story I expected to read when I began. But me getting something I did not (or forgot to) expect is not the fault of the book. <b>I should've just reread the damn synopsis like a regular person would.</b><br><br>Anyway, we follow two main protagonists:<br><br>Han, former leader of a thieving street gang, primary caretaker of his younger sister &amp; mother, curious type willing to take possession of any ol' amulet even though might potentially kill him.<br><br>Rasia, princess heir to the Fells, cares about making the lives of her citizens better, has too many love interests. <br><br>Both of these protagonists are, predictably, 15-17 years of age.<br><br>I feel mostly indifferent about both of them. Their personalities end up feeling inevitable because I've seen them so many times before. No one is unbearable to read about, and both have plenty of potential to grow into people I may care about in the future, but for now they're <b>just sort of there</b> for me. <br><br>I've talked about this before, but one thing I usually can't deal with in Young Adult books is unrealistic characterization vs age. Han apparently accomplished status as a gang leader, lived it up, and decided to retire from that life all before fully completing puberty. And I just??? <br><br><i>Why do we keep doing things like this, authors?</i> <br><br>This is part of the reason I couldn't fully take <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/23437156.Six_of_Crows__Six_of_Crows___1_" title="Six of Crows (Six of Crows, #1) by Leigh Bardugo" rel="nofollow noopener">Six of Crows</a> by <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/4575289.Leigh_Bardugo" title="Leigh Bardugo" rel="nofollow noopener">Leigh Bardugo</a> seriously either, though that book is much better than this one on many fronts. <br><br>But I always get this disjointed feeling when I am <b>told</b> I'm supposed to view 12-17 year old characters as hardened, badass, criminal types, but conversely <b>shown</b> they still possess an overwhelmingly juvenile mindset. <br><br>Around halfway through, there is a scene that squicked me out which involved a male character copping a feel of a female character's ass. In response, the female victim... well she proceeds to have sympathetic thoughts about the male character &amp; how he's probably misunderstood. He's even on the board as a love interest in some capacity. <br><br>Uhm, no? <b>*huge sigh*</b><br><br>I'm just tired of things like this, friends. <i>It's not cute, it's gross.</i><br><br>Even when individual situations between characters are meant to be dramatic or interesting, <b>I just could not force myself to engage.</b><br><br>This was my face while I trekked my way through this book:<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1440106208ra/15930293.gif" width="500" height="227" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"> <br><br>The only thing I truly liked here was the political elements (surprise, surprise). <br><br>I wanted to hear more about the war in the South &amp; the details of the conflict. I wanted to see more of the relationship between the people of the Clans and the people of Fellsmarch. I wanted <b>more worldbuilding.</b> <br><br>But unfortunately, time that could've been spent further developing the landscape of this series was wasted on silly relationship nonsense &amp; small scale conflicts, neither of which captured my interest in any meaningful capacity. <br><br>I've heard from many fans that this first book is difficult to get through, but I am concerned that the parts most people found difficult are the only parts I seemed to care about (aka the political situation). I may get around to trying out <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/7801229.The_Exiled_Queen__Seven_Realms___2_" title="The Exiled Queen (Seven Realms, #2) by Cinda Williams Chima" rel="nofollow noopener">The Exiled Queen</a>, I may not. <b>Either way, a pretty disappointing beginning.</b><br><br>Buddy read this with the gorgeous <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/user/show/42780417-fables-wren" rel="nofollow noopener">Wren</a>! Here's a link to <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1659074503?book_show_action=false&amp;from_review_page=1" rel="nofollow noopener">her review</a>, if you're interested. ♥</span>
  <a data-text-id="17411223366575755099" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

Especially a kick-butt high fantasy like this one.<br /><br />Chima has masterfully created an intriguing world, with a cast full of memorable characters.<br /><br />The chapters somewhat alternate between Han and Raisa. <div id="review_78280474" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/78280474" />
    <a title="Amy" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/2874225-amy"><img alt="Amy" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1599974197p2/2874225.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/78280474?book_show_action=true">Nov 18, 2009</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Amy" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Amy" href="/user/show/2874225-amy">Amy</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2874225-amy?shelf=oldies-still-goodies">oldies-still-goodies</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2874225-amy?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2874225-amy?shelf=ya-ya-ya">ya-ya-ya</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer78280474" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer3737563655398442395">THE DEMON KING was a perfect maelstrom of practically everything I love in a book. Court intrigue, captivating characters, intricate plotting, enticing romances, and brilliant world building coalesce to deliver the best high fantasy story EVER. <br/><br/>The characters in Chima's story are extremely well developed; each had their own unique personality that distinguished him or her as an individual entity, subsequently allowing me to easily love or hate them. In the case of Han Alister- LOVE. Han is a ref</span>
  <span id="freeText3737563655398442395" style="display:none">THE DEMON KING was a perfect maelstrom of practically everything I love in a book. Court intrigue, captivating characters, intricate plotting, enticing romances, and brilliant world building coalesce to deliver the best high fantasy story EVER. <br /><br />The characters in Chima's story are extremely well developed; each had their own unique personality that distinguished him or her as an individual entity, subsequently allowing me to easily love or hate them. In the case of Han Alister- LOVE. Han is a reformed streetlord who has a hard exterior but a heart of damn gold on the inside. It's cute. Trust me. Princess Raisa ana'Marianna is headstrong and independent and occasionally annoying in her tendency to want things <i>her</i> way, but then again- she is a princess. And because she is a princess, there are duties aplenty that await her when she comes of age and strict rules everywhere to prevent her from ever stepping out of line--it is evident that she chafes under these restraints and so therefore when she finds ways to evade these expectations and find adventures on her own or defy the rules, it's extremely satisfying and adds even more excitement to the plot. These are the two main characters but there is also a diverse array of other well fleshed-out characters that give the story greater color and taste.<br /><br />The story is told in the alternating viewpoints of Han and Raisa, with an occasional insertion of the viewpoint of other, slightly less major characters. If I had to describe the story in one sentence, I couldn't. The subplots merge and diverge; they tell separate stories of Han and Raisa and the hardships they face, and occasionally combine in the chance occasions when their paths meet. Because this is the first of a trilogy, Han and Raisa do not quite get to ah, know each other's true identity yet, but this only adds to the thrill of the story and to my keen anticipation for book 2. <br /><br />One of my favorite parts of the story was the wonderful world building that happens. Wow- this world that Chima has created is so resoundingly real in its descriptions and traditions and people. It is reminiscent of Tamora Pierce's works in several ways, and because personally I am a huge fan of Pierce, this could only add to my love of the story. For example, there is, in this story, the inclusion of street gangs, and thiefs, and temples, and lively and diverse and vibrant cities full of trade and corruption and poverty and splendor and legends, all juxtaposed to forge a unique identity that cement the magnificent world building at work here. If and when you read this book, you will be immersed in this world as you turn the pages and when the story ends, you might very well be reluctant to bid this world farewell and re-enter the real one. I know I was. <br /><br />I've always been a fan of books with court intrigue and other courtly functions, and this book does not disappoint. There are irresistible wizards and gallant soldiers, secret escapades in the night and intoxicating flirts, extravagant balls and pretty dresses. The romantic scenes in this book, when they do occur, are extremely satisfying to read. But okay, before this starts sounding like a Harlequin romance, let me tell you- it's not. The inclusion of these romantic aspects lend an air of the game of flirting and politics that is rife among any royal court in any land or any story. This is mostly in Raisa's portion of the story, but in Han's end there is romance as well. <br /><br />This review does not do the book justice, period. I've tried my best to convey the sense of wonder and love and interest I felt while reading this book, only to succeed with paltry results. Nevertheless, this book is the perfect fit for fantasy readers as well as everyone else out there. Highly recommended.</span>
  <a data-text-id="3737563655398442395" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_1854652381" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1854652381" />
    <a title="Jiana" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/10502567-jiana"><img alt="Jiana" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1540380229p2/10502567.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1854652381?book_show_action=true">Feb 28, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Jiana" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Jiana" href="/user/show/10502567-jiana">Jiana</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="did not like it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">did not like it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="ebook 9781423136149" href="/book/show/7885310-the-demon-king">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1854652381" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer3508502408494688864"><b>1.5 Stars</b><br/><br/>Buddy read with <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/user/show/57334157-caitlin' rel='nofollow noopener'>Cait</a>, who liked it way more than I did. If you want to check out her positive review, <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1857773309' rel='nofollow noopener'>here</a> it is.<br/><br/>I DID IT. I FINISHED IT. MY SUFFERING IS OVER. <br/><br/>I should've just DNFed this. I'll be honest, I did consider doing it a few times, but noooooo, I had to give it a chance. I kept on hoping it'd get better. But nope.<br/><br/>Nope.<br/>Nope.<br/>Nope.<br/><br/>Obviously, I'm an unpopular opinion here since this has a 4.20 average rating. But oh. It wasn't my cup of tea.<br/><br/><b>I'm just SO SAD AND ANGRY AND DISAPPOINT</b></span>
  <span id="freeText3508502408494688864" style="display:none"><b>1.5 Stars</b><br /><br />Buddy read with <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/user/show/57334157-caitlin" rel="nofollow noopener">Cait</a>, who liked it way more than I did. If you want to check out her positive review, <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1857773309" rel="nofollow noopener">here</a> it is.<br /><br />I DID IT. I FINISHED IT. MY SUFFERING IS OVER. <br /><br />I should've just DNFed this. I'll be honest, I did consider doing it a few times, but noooooo, I had to give it a chance. I kept on hoping it'd get better. But nope.<br /><br />Nope.<br />Nope.<br />Nope.<br /><br />Obviously, I'm an unpopular opinion here since this has a 4.20 average rating. But oh. It wasn't my cup of tea.<br /><br /><b>I'm just SO SAD AND ANGRY AND DISAPPOINTED.</b> Do you know how excited I was?! I was <i>so</i> damn excited. Caitlin and I were so excited to read it and buy the boxset. <i>I needed this to be good so I could buy the boxset, man.</i> Caitlin really enjoyed the book and told me I'd have to push through the first 10 chapters because they are slow and confusing and then the book would get really good. And so I did. Did the book get any better? Not for me. Here, I started considering DNFing it and even Cait encouraged me because she knew it wasn't going to get better for me past that point. Oh well. <br /><br />I DON'T KNOW HOW TO EVEN REVIEW THIS. It was so, so, so, <b>uttely</b> slow and boring. I could go on and on about how boring it is and it still wouldn't describe how boring it was for me. It was mind numbing. I get that first books in series are usually slow because of all the world-building and that, but it's not okay for me when the entirety of the book is boring as all hell. At first, I was enjoying the female MCs chapters, but then I quickly lost interest. <br /><br />Now. The world-building. Oh my God. I also understand when world-building is confusing at first. It's normal. But this way too confusing and overwhelming. Everything was confusing! I was lost during most of the book. Personally, I don't think Cinda Williams Chima did the best job explaining the overall world. Don't get wrong, I did understand things here and there; I wasn't completely oblivious. But I shouldn't reach the end of the book still unsure if I understand the world right. I shouldn't feel overwhelmed throughout the entirety of a book.<br /><br />The MCs, Han and Raisa were just... well, I don't really care about either of them. I felt no connection to either of them. I never cared about Han, not for one chapter even. His chapters were the most confusing and I didn't understand where his plot was going. Raisa's chapters were much easier, but did I care? Nope. As I stated before, I was actually enjoying her chapters at first. They gave me Falling Kingdoms vibes, but then I quickly lost interest and I didn't give a damn about Raisa wanting to rebel against her family's wishes and the Queendom's rules or all the boys she's kissed (I'm not against that - she can kiss whoever she wants, but every time Raisa introduced some boy, it would be a boy she shared a few kisses with here and there. Is there nothing more to say about said boy??????). As for the side characters, I also didn't give a damn about any. I liked Amon at first. He reminded me of Chaol (Throne of Glass) and Theon (Falling Kingdoms) and I quickly liked him. But once again, I quickly lost interest. <br /><br />The plot... was there really a plot? It was just small random subplots here and there. No big conflict. EVERYTHING WAS SO BLAND. Nothing big was happening. It was just random events being told. GAH. I think the actual plot started with the last two chapters. <i>Too late.</i> Chima's writing was personally bland. It didn't hold my attention and I basically got distracted 1827832 times reading this. I'd literally wake up, read a bit, end up falling asleep again. Wow.<br /><br /><b>All in all: boring, bland, nothing special.</b><br /><br />GAHKADFHJKDDSJFJDS. I'm so disappointed. I wanted to love this! I was so sure I would. I even read reviews of people comparing it to Falling Kingdoms and I <b>loved</b> Falling Kingdoms. I gave it 5 stars... but GAH. OH WELL. I'm still sad, okay. I do understand why people would've enjoyed it, I think it had lots of potential, but again the execution was lacking in all areas. Maybe the series gets way better and an actual plot develops and occurs. Will I give the second book a try? Nope. <b>BYE, BOOK.</b><br /><br /><b>
  <u>Pre-review:</u>
</b><br /><br />I'm super excited for this and I JUST <i>NEED</i> THIS TO BE GOOD. Please don't disappoint.</span>

<div id="review_2299977116" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2299977116" />
    <a title="Tani" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/63414753-tani"><img alt="Tani" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1521292450p2/63414753.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2299977116?book_show_action=true">Apr 12, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Tani" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Tani" href="/user/show/63414753-tani">Tani</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9781423121367" href="/book/show/7479205-the-demon-king">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/63414753-tani?shelf=favorites">favorites</a>
          </div>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2299977116" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer5948007472800610792">RATINGS: 4 STARS. <br/><br/><br/>“Hanalea's Bloody Bones!!!!”<br/><br/><br/>Finally, I've found myself to be crazy about a book after a very long time. I had lot of anticipation of the book because I had procrastinated to read it for a while. I've tried my level best to hate this book, but unfortunately I couldn't. I know many of them hated the slow pace of the book but I think patience is a must to read this book as it was worth it. At the beginning, the description about the kingdom, clans, history, geography, etc. were to</span>
  <span id="freeText5948007472800610792" style="display:none">RATINGS: 4 STARS. <br /><br /><br />“Hanalea's Bloody Bones!!!!”<br /><br /><br />Finally, I've found myself to be crazy about a book after a very long time. I had lot of anticipation of the book because I had procrastinated to read it for a while. I've tried my level best to hate this book, but unfortunately I couldn't. I know many of them hated the slow pace of the book but I think patience is a must to read this book as it was worth it. At the beginning, the description about the kingdom, clans, history, geography, etc. were too tedious for reading but eventually as the story progressed the attention - grabbing grip of this story increased. It is later realised that the lengthy details given are important, too. I'm overwhelmed with curiosity to continue this series due to the cliffhanger. So who cares whether the story was slow paced or fast paced if one’s going to get an amazing story in return? <br /><br /><br /><br />This is the beginning of the saga about Hanson Alister a.k.a Hunts Alone a.k.a Hans a.k.a Cuffs, a former street lord of Raggers, who lives his life by earning daily bread and butter by doing odd jobs and Princess Raisa ana’ Marianna, the heir of the Grey Wolf throne of the Fellsmarch, who has returned to her kingdom after living with Demonai clan. It was entwined with a revered legend about the terrible ‘Breaking’ occurred after the use of dark magic by the Demon King followed by the destruction of the Demon King by Princess Hanalea ana’ Maria, the last queen of the old line of the Grey Wolf throne of the Fellsmarch. Their tale was expected to be the triumph of the good over the evil only but there was more to it.<br /><br /><br /><br />“History. Why do we need to know what happened before we were born?”<br />“So hopefully we get smarter and don't make the same mistakes again.”<br /><br /><br /><br />Hans Allister, a former leader of gang, is guilt- ridden for his past actions and tries his best to keep his family safe and sound. His life is mixed with dangerous threats as he’s still recognised as the leader. He was a grifter. He has a pair of cuffs, each on his either hands, which is considered to be magical as they've changed their sizes throughout his entire life since his birth. One day, he takes an amulet from Micah Bayar, son of the High Wizard, to protect his friend and himself from further harm by the wizard. Later, it is revealed to be similar to the amulet of the infamous wizard, the Demon King. <br /><br /><br /><br />“Take the charge of the horse you're riding before you try to rein in someone else's.”<br /><br /><br /><br />Princess Raisa was enigmatic, headstrong and fiery girl who was driven by her ambition for the welfare of her kingdom and a strong urge to find freedom for herself. One might consider her as outrageously rebellious but I think she's just a girl who doesn't want luxuries and comfort as she was born in royalty but earn her own respect and strength over the kingdom by sympathising the people and being vigilant to bring the prosperity to her kingdom. She tries her best to warn Queen Marianna, her mother, about forthcoming threats on the kingdom but her mother turns a blind eye towards it.<br /><br /><br /><br />Initially, the book felt it was dragging every ounce of patience and tolerance within me but I kept reading because I didn't want to leave it unread and lose a chance for getting to know what exactly made some of my friends like this book. At last, I was very wrong to consider it was boring. The turn of the events when the protagonists meet for the first time dumbfounded me. Seriously, that was unexpectedly surprising. I felt more connected to Raisa than Han. I liked that the queens were given more importance in the royal line which is unique. After almost 35 % of the book, the story kept up increasing its tempo till the end. The cliffhanger made me to like this entire book and actually understand everything that was left unexplained. The climax of the story created internal conflict of emotions within me because at first I was definitely going to give a negative review but I couldn't after reading everything.<br /><br /><br /><br />The characters had depth and intriguing spark with their own charisma which kept building up. The flow of the writing was captivating as the story begins to be interesting. The conversation / dialogues were good enough for the story. The world building was mesmerizing and vibrant. The overall plot was dynamic and exhilarating. The novelty in the story was that both the protagonists had different lives and almost nothing was common between them. The protagonists are together in the book for almost 10% or less.<br /><br /><br /><br />About the flaws, I felt the book could've been improved a bit. The starting of the book was the main drawback. But considering most of the fantasy series’ first book don't create a wham- bam great impressions, I felt this book was lot better comparatively. There wasn’t any cheesy and mushy romance. Instead we get acquainted with the characters a lot. It has no love at first sight or insta- love. If anyone’s up for a fantasy book with no insta- love, no irrational melodrama and no over and above ridiculousness, the book can be a fun for reading.<br /><br /><br />Thanks for reading my review. Happy Reading!!!  😊</span>
  <a data-text-id="5948007472800610792" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1693004808" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1693004808" />
    <a title="Zain Otoom" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/45136398-zain-otoom"><img alt="Zain Otoom" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1598878687p2/45136398.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1693004808?book_show_action=true">Nov 11, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Zain Otoom" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Zain Otoom" href="/user/show/45136398-zain-otoom">Zain Otoom</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1693004808" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer11221536919817296232"><b>
  <i>SPOILER-FREE REVIEW!</i>
</b><br/>I really enjoyed this book. It wasn't what I expected but nonetheless, it was good. This book is so slow at the beginning. It picks up roughly after chapter 12/13, or page 200 or so. It's definitely a build up book. There's so much world building in this book it's crazy, and I have to say, it was one of my favorite parts about this book. I listened to most of this book on audiobook because I was struggling to get into it, so if you seem to have the same problem, I recomme</span>
  <span id="freeText11221536919817296232" style="display:none"><b>
  <i>SPOILER-FREE REVIEW!</i>
</b><br />I really enjoyed this book. It wasn't what I expected but nonetheless, it was good. This book is so slow at the beginning. It picks up roughly after chapter 12/13, or page 200 or so. It's definitely a build up book. There's so much world building in this book it's crazy, and I have to say, it was one of my favorite parts about this book. I listened to most of this book on audiobook because I was struggling to get into it, so if you seem to have the same problem, I recommend listening to the audiobook instead. The narrator is quite good!<br />Now I'd like to talk about the characters:<br /><b>Raisa</b> <br />I like Raisa a lot. Her personality is explosive, she's stubborn and strong-willed. Even if you might feel like a boy who thinks himself a little handsome might sway her in anything involving her Queendom, you're wrong. She enjoys the company and silly dates and stolen kisses, but she's a future warrior queen, alright. She's spunky and clever and has her wits about her which I really liked. I see a huge character development that Raisa will go through and, oh I can't wait. <br />One thing though, why is she like 15? That's too young, but what am I to say when I'm 16 myself. <br /><b>Han</b> <br />Even though I preferred Raisa's pov over his, I still enjoyed it. Though, I find Han to be more of a little lost puppy than a former streetlord. Not that he's not badass or anything, but he's just too sweet. When someone says streetlord, I think of a cunning asshole who has no conscience with a maddening level of genius. But I guess that just me. He doesn't seem to think sometimes, but I tried to keep in mind his own situation and the way his life is. Lies, mistrust, abuse, grief and some loneliness, and let's not forget the fact he's just 16. I'm glad he has Dancer to be his friend. <br /><b>Amon</b> <br />I love him? I found him really comfortable and really caring for Raisa. And even though you see from his perspective only twice, he truly makes an intriguing character, and I wish to know more about him. Honestly? Despite the predictable nature of the romance, I wouldn't mind if Raisa ended up with him.<br />All the other characters—expect Amon's father, Raisa's and Dancer—were annoying as fuck, as they were meant to be. So bravo, Chima, you succeeded in creating insufferable characters. From her fuckity the Queen to that asshole Bayar and his son. Micah is such a tool. I hate weak tools who have no character beyond their outer looks. <br /><b>World Building</b><br />It's so complex and interesting, and so full of things I have yet to learn. It's evident that the author spent time actually thinking of the world. From politics to the really intriguing magic system, and to the intricate history full of lies and deception, consider me amazed. I didn't find myself bored whatsoever reading the parts that involved world building. So well done. <br /><b>The Plot</b><br />This book is just a build up for the main plot. An evident plot doesn't appear in this book till the very last end. Not to say it's entirely boring, not at all, but you do have to be patient. There are, of course, parts where I found to useless to the plot, but they were good for character introduction. I feel like I truly, now, know both world and characters well enough to get to the butter of this series. And boy does it sound promising. <br />***<br />All in all, I do recommend this book to anyone with enough patience, because I'm sure you'll rewarded with a really good and unforgettable YA fantasy series.<br />I will definitely continue this series on, and soon, I hope!</span>
  <a data-text-id="11221536919817296232" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1419064636" />
    <a title="Lexie" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/20726801-lexie"><img alt="Lexie" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1524678402p2/20726801.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1419064636?book_show_action=true">Oct 17, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Lexie" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Lexie" href="/user/show/20726801-lexie">Lexie</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>


          <div><span class="uitext greyText">Recommends it for: </span>
           <span class="uitext reviewText">Wizards, street rats, warriors, and aspiring Overlords</span></div>

          <div>
    <span class="greyText">Recommended to Lexie by: </span>
      <a href="/user/show/11375137-c-g-drews">C.G. Drews</a>
  </div>


          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/20726801-lexie?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/20726801-lexie?shelf=read-in-2016">read-in-2016</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1419064636" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer16600084466998733277">Reviewed at <a href='http://thehonestbookclub.blogspot.rs/2016/02/book-review-demon-king-by-cinda.html' rel='nofollow noopener'>The Honest Bookclub</a>.<br/><br/><b>4.5</b><br/><br/><b>Han Alister:</b><br/>•	a drifter and a grifter<br/>•	a life of perpetual uncertainty<br/>•	a home he can't visit and a foster camp he can't call home.<br/><br/><b>Raisa ana'Marianna:</b><br/>•	a princess<br/>•	a life planned for her before she was even born<br/>•	a home she can't leave, far from a camp she calls her real home.<br/><br/><br/>Han and Raisa are about to meet - in a world brought down by wizards but where wizards rule from the shadows, and in queendom run by a queen who circumvents conflict. They'll meet in stree</span>
  <span id="freeText16600084466998733277" style="display:none">Reviewed at <a href="http://thehonestbookclub.blogspot.rs/2016/02/book-review-demon-king-by-cinda.html" rel="nofollow noopener">The Honest Bookclub</a>.<br /><br /><b>4.5</b><br /><br /><b>Han Alister:</b><br />•	a drifter and a grifter<br />•	a life of perpetual uncertainty<br />•	a home he can't visit and a foster camp he can't call home.<br /><br /><b>Raisa ana'Marianna:</b><br />•	a princess<br />•	a life planned for her before she was even born<br />•	a home she can't leave, far from a camp she calls her real home.<br /><br /><br />Han and Raisa are about to meet - in a world brought down by wizards but where wizards rule from the shadows, and in queendom run by a queen who circumvents conflict. They'll meet in street-gang territory where street gangs are the least dangerous denizen. And though Han and Raisa's worlds are about to collide, their stories will unveil separately.<br /><br />Needless to say, <i>The Demon King</i> is a wonderful mass of contradictions. Its biggest contradiction to date is how good it is, and how it never quite got the acclaim that it deserves.<br /><br />(Based on book one, at the very least.)<br /><br />Before I get into any aspect of the story, I will be kind and generous and impart this great advice - <b>STAY AWAY FROM THE SYNOPSIS</b>. This, of course, varies depending on which edition of the book you have (or which edition you look up on Goodreads). But the synopsis on the back cover of my book (bought as a box set, to whom it may concern) was <i>so needlessly detailed</i> that it revealed half of the book's plot, and pretty much gave me a rundown of all the plot twists meant to take me by surprise. If ever there was a series where knowing less is more, this is it. <b>The synopsis is your enemy.</b> If you aren't best friends with spoilers, at any rate. Now... *clears throat* Moving on to the book praise.<br /><br />First off, I am biased. I am biased as heck about this series. Fantasy is my literary home. It's where I run when things get really scary in other genres (only to be re-traumatized by fantasy in turn - but that's a self-inflicted, masochistic sort of thing). This is mostly because I find that when fantasy fails, it doesn't often fail as dramatically as other genres. A fantasy book/series <i>can</i> go wrong, of course. There are almost mapped pitfalls where it can hit a snag and drag, drag, drag.<br /><br />The Demon King, needless to say, didn't. And witnessing it swerve around the pitfalls was <i>beautiful</i>.<br /><br />•	<b>Some of the time, the world and the overall plot in fantasy serve as a kind of muted, faded backdrop for the rampant romance in the forefront. <u>The Demon King doesn't.</u></b> (If you're noticing a theme here... the theme is noticing you back and winking. It's wearing glitter, so you know it isn't going for subtle.) Sometimes I will still read a romancey fantasy series, because I'm a hypocrite who basks in their own hypocrisy. But most of the time, I'll feel cheated. The Demon King follows two separate protagonist in same, yet vastly different worlds, as they fight their vastly different battles. The natural assumption is that they will naturally meet and interact. And so they shall. But if you're expecting awkward teenage sexual tension and dream sequences where <i>that was the first night Raisa dreamed of Han Alister</i> - HA. That's my professional assessment - HA. Make of that what you will.<br />•	<b>Alternatively, fantasy can be slow. <u>The Demon King... you guessed it, isn't.</u></b> In the interest of not spoiling you to anything beyond chapter one, I will say that in this first chapter alone, there are wizards, a forest fire, a standoff, a making of arch nemeses, cursed talismans, and a mention of demons. So there.<br /><br />These, incidentally, aren't even the highlights. The highlights, in my fantasy-loving heavily-biased opinion stand thusly:<br />•	<s>I love the worst thusly and it's a highlight in and of itself.</s><br />•	<b>Queens, wizards and shamans are in power. Cue epicness</b> Wizards and shamans lowkey hate each other. Cue epic power struggles.<br />•	<b>QUEENDOM! MATRIARCHY!</b> Not only is this land ruled by a long line of QUEENS, all from names to titles and status is inherited from mothers. Even in camps which adhere to very few rules of the queendom, the matriarchs are in charge, and women are beyond respected.<br />•	<b>The story touches on some themes explored in <i>The Giver</i></b> - the curse of one who sees the world for what it is clearly, and who knows it for what it was.<br />•	<b>NO ONE writes teenagers like Cinda Williams Chima.</b> Even in this charged, epic fantasy setting, the teenage characters <i>read like teenagers</i>! They aren't precocious fifty year-olds in teenage bodies. They are, you know, sixteen years old, with all its occasional awkwardness and poor decision-making. Han's relationships with his friends and his inability to find his own independent identity at times should resonate with just about every human being, if only in retrospect. Seeing Han laugh at the urban legends surrounding him and exclaiming that <i>"[He is] only sixteen, how could any of [the legends about him] be true?"</i> was a new high for me. Raisa's constant questioning and occasional spite are also quintessentially sixteen. The easiest thing to get Raisa to do something is to inform her that it's forbidden. She disappears in a poof of smoke like a cartoon character, and she's off doing it right now, immediately, this very second. She isn't every sixteen year-old, but she is in no way a wise, sensible adult. <s>(Just in case such people exist. I've heard rumors. Scary, scary rumors.)</s><br /><br />As for the bad? Well, I saw the plot twists coming from about page five. But I'm almost certain that this is the oversharing synopsis's fault far more than the book's. The synopsis is that one aunt at a family gathering who never stops talking, usually about unsightly moles and surgeries. During meals. In glorious detail.<br /><br />So avoid the synopsis, really. But absolutely give this book a chance. I hear the series gets <i>better</i> with each installment, too, not that that's even possible. But I dare you, in an official-challenge capacity, to find out alongside me. <br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="16600084466998733277" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

    <a title="Nouf *LostinFantasy*" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/33795465-nouf-lostinfantasy"><img alt="Nouf *LostinFantasy*" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1480352284p2/33795465.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/33795465-nouf-lostinfantasy?shelf=books-with-maps">books-with-maps</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/33795465-nouf-lostinfantasy?shelf=favorite-characters">favorite-characters</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/33795465-nouf-lostinfantasy?shelf=fantasy-sci-fi">fantasy-sci-fi</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/33795465-nouf-lostinfantasy?shelf=epic-fantasy">epic-fantasy</a>,

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1557412412" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer14028152622855609754">I didn't expect to enjoy this book so much but <b>I ended up loving it!</b> The world building, setting, and characters were everything I look for in a fantasy book! I guess you can say this first book in the series was pretty much 500 pages of introducing and setting up the plot. But I was still <b>completely wrapped up in the characters' adventures and how everything came together in the end! </b><br/><br/>The dark history between the wizards and the clans and the line of queens (yes, it's a queendom!) is what <b>shapes</b></span>
  <span id="freeText14028152622855609754" style="display:none">I didn't expect to enjoy this book so much but <b>I ended up loving it!</b> The world building, setting, and characters were everything I look for in a fantasy book! I guess you can say this first book in the series was pretty much 500 pages of introducing and setting up the plot. But I was still <b>completely wrapped up in the characters' adventures and how everything came together in the end! </b><br /><br />The dark history between the wizards and the clans and the line of queens (yes, it's a queendom!) is what <b>shapes the plot and secrets of the book.</b> And all the trouble and adventure kicks off when Han, one of the two main characters, takes home a magical amulet that turns out might be connected to the legend of the Demon King (the wizard that almost ended their world a thousand years before). The story is told mainly through <b>two POV's</b> -- moving between the extravagance and deceptions of royal life with <b>Princess heir, Raisa</b> (and her best friend and guard, Amon), and then the hardships of being targeted on the streets with <b>former thief, Han Alister</b>. <br /><br /><b>I liked all the characters</b>, really - even the shifty Micah. And usually I get really annoyed with romantic triangles in YA fantasy, but <b>I'm excited about all the character relationships here.</b> I shipped Raisa a little bit with all three guys in the story (not sorry). Still, those few hints and sparks of romance don't drive her actions or take over the plot. <b>I loved Raisa as the heroine of the story.</b> She's stubborn and acts like an entitled sixteen year old princess but I really like how proactive she is as a character, not allowing herself to remain a naive princess or to turn a blind eye to anything - I can really see her developing wonderfully through the series. <br /><br /><b>I'm really looking forward to seeing what happens next.</b> There's a few books I was planning on reading before continuing this series but I'm ready to pick up the next book right now despite having just spent the entire day finishing this one!<br /><br /></span>

<div id="review_1857773309" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1857773309" />
    <a title="Caitlin" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/57334157-caitlin"><img alt="Caitlin" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1507948675p2/57334157.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1857773309?book_show_action=true">Feb 28, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Caitlin" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Caitlin" href="/user/show/57334157-caitlin">Caitlin</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/57334157-caitlin?shelf=2017-read">2017-read</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/57334157-caitlin?shelf=4-stars">4-stars</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1857773309" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer15393085107053725599"><b>Buddy read</b> with <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1854652381?book_show_action=false' rel='nofollow noopener'>Jia</a>! <br/><br/>Wow. I had high hopes for this series and I was not at all disappointed. It was such a promising start to what I know will be an amazing series. This book was highly intimidating because it was high fantasy and the chapters were 20 pages long. I'll admit, I did struggle through the first 5-10 chapters because it was a lot of world building and characters to process and learn about. However, when I sat down and really dedicated my time to the book, I flew through it and adore</span>
  <span id="freeText15393085107053725599" style="display:none"><b>Buddy read</b> with <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1854652381?book_show_action=false" rel="nofollow noopener">Jia</a>! <br /><br />Wow. I had high hopes for this series and I was not at all disappointed. It was such a promising start to what I know will be an amazing series. This book was highly intimidating because it was high fantasy and the chapters were 20 pages long. I'll admit, I did struggle through the first 5-10 chapters because it was a lot of world building and characters to process and learn about. However, when I sat down and really dedicated my time to the book, I flew through it and adored it. <br /><br />I've seen some comparison to the Falling Kingdoms series and I'd definitely say that if you love Falling Kingdoms, this will be right up your alley (and vice versa). The story in both series are definitely very different but there's certainly similarities. However, there's way less death in this book - which kinda sucks. I want some crazy shit to go down and everyone just DIE. <br /><br />Okay, so for some reason I normally like male characters way more than female characters. However, I instantly formed a connection to Raisa and I adored her throughout the entire book - she's definitely my favourite character. I think this was definitely because of the fact that her story seemed to be easier to follow and even though there were lots of characters in her plot, you could still easily understand the dynamic. However, Han was definitely a more complex character. He's mixed up in a whole bunch of shit and his story isn't as easy to follow, I guess. I really struggled with his chapters for about maybe half of the book but it definitely got easier when you understood who was who and what the hell was happening in his life. When Raisa and Han met I almost screamed. I loved seeing these 2 characters meet and seeing their perspective of each other. I want to see way more of their interactions and, from the blurb of the next book, there will be lots of them together. Is it bad that I already kinda ship it? I have 0 idea about the ships but I feel like they'll be endgame and I can 10/10 be on board this.<br /><br />Look, plot wise this book is pretty fast paced when it gets into it - even though it has a bit of a slow start. I enjoyed seeing the dynamic between all of the characters and what the hell is going on in this mess of a Queendom. Overall, this book was great and I can't wait to see what's to come!</span>
  <a data-text-id="15393085107053725599" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_124357148" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/124357148" />
    <a title="Stacia (the 2010 club)" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4013351-stacia-the-2010-club"><img alt="Stacia (the 2010 club)" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1417661051p2/4013351.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/124357148?book_show_action=true">Oct 01, 2010</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Stacia (the 2010 club)" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Stacia (the 2010 club)" href="/user/show/4013351-stacia-the-2010-club">Stacia (the 2010 club)</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4013351-stacia-the-2010-club?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>,

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer124357148" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer15340247940886793712">I have the hardest time reviewing fantasy books. I'm not sure why this is. Maybe because so much is constantly going on, it leaves me a bit stumped as to how to summarize everything in an eloquent fashion.<br/><br/>Fans of traditional fantasy, whether it be adult or YA, will most likely appreciate this series. The Demon King read very much like a slightly scaled down version of a good adult epic fantasy - not much was held back for the sake of a younger audience.<br/><br/>From the good to the evil characters, I fou</span>
  <span id="freeText15340247940886793712" style="display:none">I have the hardest time reviewing fantasy books. I'm not sure why this is. Maybe because so much is constantly going on, it leaves me a bit stumped as to how to summarize everything in an eloquent fashion.<br /><br />Fans of traditional fantasy, whether it be adult or YA, will most likely appreciate this series. The Demon King read very much like a slightly scaled down version of a good adult epic fantasy - not much was held back for the sake of a younger audience.<br /><br />From the good to the evil characters, I found most, if not all, of them interesting. This doesn't happen often for me in books, which makes me look forward to reading the next installment.<br /><br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="15340247940886793712" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

<div id="review_1175895554" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1175895554" />
    <a title="Chelsea ❤Peril Please❤ " class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/8422853-chelsea-peril-please"><img alt="Chelsea ❤Peril Please❤ " src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1570038444p2/8422853.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1175895554?book_show_action=true">Jan 21, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Chelsea ❤Peril Please❤ " class="user" itemprop="url" name="Chelsea ❤Peril Please❤ " href="/user/show/8422853-chelsea-peril-please">Chelsea ❤Peril Please❤ </a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/8422853-chelsea-peril-please?shelf=physical-book-wishlist-want-it-need">physical-book-wishlist-want-it-need</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/8422853-chelsea-peril-please?shelf=favorites">favorites</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/8422853-chelsea-peril-please?shelf=my-favorite-covers">my-favorite-covers</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/8422853-chelsea-peril-please?shelf=alternating-pov">alternating-pov</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/8422853-chelsea-peril-please?shelf=could-read-over-and-over-again">could-read-over-and-over-again</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/8422853-chelsea-peril-please?shelf=unforgettable-male-leads">unforgettable-male-leads</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/8422853-chelsea-peril-please?shelf=epic-reads-for-light-and-dark-pup">epic-reads-for-light-and-dark-pup</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1175895554" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer9480315003961026667"><br/><b>
  <i>
    <blockquote>He called her Briar Rose, he said, because of her beauty. And her many thorns.<blockquote></blockquote>
</blockquote>
  </i>
</b><br/><br/>It's not often that I find a YA fantasy series that enraptures me the way this one did. It's no secret that I am <i>very</i> picky when it comes to reading these, as well. Needless to say, I've been side-eyeing this series for FOREVER, yet I have never taken the plunge. I've mentioned it to a couple of my closest friends and have felt there was something special about it for a long while. So why not leap right in</span>
  <span id="freeText9480315003961026667" style="display:none"><br><b>
  <i>
    <blockquote>He called her Briar Rose, he said, because of her beauty. And her many thorns.<blockquote></blockquote>
</blockquote>
  </i>
</b><br><br>It's not often that I find a YA fantasy series that enraptures me the way this one did. It's no secret that I am <i>very</i> picky when it comes to reading these, as well. Needless to say, I've been side-eyeing this series for FOREVER, yet I have never taken the plunge. I've mentioned it to a couple of my closest friends and have felt there was something special about it for a long while. So why not leap right in then? I don't know...because I'm <i>stupid</i>???<br><br>There comes a time when <b>my cautious nature and blurred lines cause a lot of missed opportunities</b>, and this one is by far one of the greatest. Had my great friend, <b>Jen</b>, not bought me this for my birthday (among many others, sigh, spoiled), it might have even been another year before I even <i>considered</i> it again. I go through phases, ya know? So, anyway, here comes my husband's family vacation and I know I will likely have time to basque in the glory that is no drowsiness from work. Whatever should I read, I thought? Well, this one was on my list. My only mistake (besides having to listen to people incessantly talking in my ear 24/7 whilst I tried to cram read)? Saving this one for the end of the week.<br><br>Or was that a gift in disguise? It's also no secret that I found another series I absolutely fucking adored from the minute I picked it up, enrapturing me for 90% of the trip, and for that I can't say I made many mistakes. However, I do regret only having a couple days, in the end, of Han time. Because I waited, though, here I am getting to post a more coherent review than any of my poor <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/7129598.Nevermore__Nevermore___1_" title="Nevermore (Nevermore, #1) by Kelly Creagh" rel="nofollow noopener">Nevermore</a> books did, and that breaks my heart, because there will never be enough time in my life to go back and re-write all those mini-reviews. I do plan to add quotes to them ALL, though, so be warned *pointy finger emoji*. <br><br>ANYWAY, my time is winding down even as I dawdle on meaningless chit chat. All I really wanted to portray in this review for my great friends is this: This story was addicting beyond words, creative beyond measure, and <b>Han will steal your heart</b> before you even realize the little thief has weaseled his way into your soul-He has an uncanny knack for such things. And, hey, even better, he hasn't even fully developed into the hero I know (and hear, from a little snake/Dark Pup) he will become. I can't even WAIT for book three and four (YES, I AM DONE WITH BOOK TWO). <br><br><b>
  <blockquote>He was not the sort to try and reconcile the warring souls that lived inside his body. <br>There was Han Alister, son and big brother, breadwinner, deal-maker, and small-time conniver. There was Hunts Alone, who'd been adopted by Marisa Pines and wished he could melt into the clans for good. And finally, Cuffs, petty criminal and street fighter, onetime streetlord of the Ragger gang and enemy of the Southies. <br>From day to day he slid out of one skin and pulled on another. No wonder it was hard to sort out who he was.</blockquote>
</b><br><br>So why only four, you ask, while I wrap up this pitiful mini-review? I can't be sure other than the fact that maybe I wanted a little more, in the end. For a fantasy, <b>I found this book was</b> not boring, but, in fact, <b>unputdownable</b>. From the beginning I was captured in it's alluring web with no way out, and Han was nipping at my heels, making my heart beat faster than I could have possibly expected. But then, at the end (and maybe I was tired), I wanted more as the last 20% began to unwind. Oh yeah-I'm saving that last star for the last two books. Let's hope they impress me in ways I can't fathom, at this point. <br><br><b>Peril?</b> Oh boy, this series is guna have it in spades.<br><b>Romance?</b> I CAN'T EVEN.<br><b>World? </b> What's not to love?<br><br>I dunno. This isn't what I wanted for ANY of my reviews in the last week, but at least this one got some more from me than just 'oh my GAWD, I can't even.' *shrugs*<br><br><br><i>For more of my reviews, please visit:</i><br><a href="http://starcrossedbookblog.com/chelsea-peril-please-reviews/" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1452287303i/17673713._SX540_.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><a title="Facebook" href="https://www.facebook.com/starcrossedbookblog" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1438055977i/15660595.png" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a> <a title="Twitter" href="https://twitter.com/starcrossedblog" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1438055639i/15660580.png" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a> <a title="RSS" href="http://feeds.feedburner.com/starcrossedbookblog/METU" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1438055639i/15660581.png" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a> <a title="BLOGLOVIN" href="https://www.bloglovin.com/blogs/star-crossed-book-blog-13035961" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1438055639i/15660579.png" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a> <a title="Google+" href="https://plus.google.com/u/0/b/116866754719786372049/+Starcrossedbookblog/posts" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1439651670i/15866819.png" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><br>******************************<br>This. Book. Was. <i>Excellent </i>! I can't even begin to explain how happy I am that I loved this...I've been eyeing it for years and finally my lovely Jen took fate out of my hands and got it for me for my birthday...THANK YOU, LOVELY!!!! I ADORED this.<br><br><br> HANNNNNNNNN.!!!! Onto book two...so frikkin' excited I read this on my vacation. :D<br><br>RTC! *fingers crossed* hopefully...<br></span>
  <a data-text-id="9480315003961026667" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

<div id="review_591804964" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/591804964" />
    <a title="Hershey " class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/19468761-hershey"><img alt="Hershey " src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1599546236p2/19468761.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/591804964?book_show_action=true">Apr 16, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Hershey " class="user" itemprop="url" name="Hershey " href="/user/show/19468761-hershey">Hershey </a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="ebook 9781423136149" href="/book/show/7885310-the-demon-king">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/19468761-hershey?shelf=high-fantasy">high-fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/19468761-hershey?shelf=quite-awesome">quite-awesome</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/19468761-hershey?shelf=disappointed-in-you">disappointed-in-you</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/19468761-hershey?shelf=fun-fun-fun">fun-fun-fun</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer591804964" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer11061536899531714253"><b> <i> “History,' Mari muttered, as if she'd overheard his thoughts. 'Why do we need to know what happened before we were born?' <br/><br/>'So hopefully we get smarter and don't make the same mistakes again.” </i></b> <br/><br/><img src='https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1380222758ra/501299.gif' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/>____________________________________________<br/><br/>This book was really good. Don't let my three stars dampen your spirit for reading this book.<br/><br/><b> The Demon King </b> was an enjoyable read. I cannot say that this book completely blew me away but it was surprising and interesting. Hunts Alone aka Hans Alister was an a</span>
  <span id="freeText11061536899531714253" style="display:none"><b> <i> “History,' Mari muttered, as if she'd overheard his thoughts. 'Why do we need to know what happened before we were born?' <br><br>'So hopefully we get smarter and don't make the same mistakes again.” </i></b> <br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1380222758ra/501299.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>____________________________________________<br><br>This book was really good. Don't let my three stars dampen your spirit for reading this book.<br><br><b> The Demon King </b> was an enjoyable read. I cannot say that this book completely blew me away but it was surprising and interesting. Hunts Alone aka Hans Alister was an amazing protagonist! He was one of the main reasons that I liked this book. <br><br>I have mixed feelings about this book. There were many instances when I kept thinking that this book was like any other book with a predictable plot and characters. It was in the end that I realized, even though it was predictable and all, I still enjoyed reading it. <br><br>I took my dear time reading this one and I guess I would have liked this book more if I had read it in one sitting. Dragging this book is not a good idea. You might get bored with the characters and the plot. Well, I did. I don't know about you but I would suggest you read it quickly. It is a fast - paced book and it requires a fast - paced reader.<br><br>One of the other reasons I liked this book was because of the element of magic in it. Though it didn't play a very significant role, I was hooked whenever the wizards were mentioned. I love magic and it will always intrigue me. Also, there isn't much of romance it and it was relieving. At least, I didn't have to constantly think about who ends up with who though I am curious whom one of the characters will end up with but it's not constantly on my mind :D<br><br>The main reason why I didn't give this book four or five stars is because of the story line. The characters where amazing but there wasn't a good story line to support them. It was a bit cliched and all but nothing so bad you can't read it. <br><br>I hope the second installment is better than the first one. The Demon King is a good read. Not exceptional or great but good. </span>
  <a data-text-id="11061536899531714253" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('vQh7VHg7W7QAhAb9K2BHVT/sHDO80PFUjBP/1GHtjumY/NAeStT6qAq5iID2QflibGrQaxefK1lqxAH0pSUJqw==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('SQE2lrubOGcinH5CeJMF46GeMwNeVHNeAwFrwMn73Axs9Z3ciXSZeyih8D+lsrvU8hj/W/UbqVPl1pXgDTNbTg==')})
  }

<div class='bookAuthorProfile__about'>

<span id="freeTextContainer2139660312379653065">New York Times bestselling author Cinda Williams Chima comes from a long line of fortune-tellers, musicians and spinners of tales. She began writing romance novels in middle school, which were often confiscated by her teachers.<br/><br/>Her Heir Chronicles series (magic comes to contemporary Ohio) comprises <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/213647.The_Warrior_Heir' title='The Warrior Heir' rel='nofollow noopener'>The Warrior Heir</a> <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/500743.The_Wizard_Heir' title='The Wizard Heir' rel='nofollow noopener'>The Wizard Heir</a> . <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/2866413.The_Dragon_Heir' title='The Dragon Heir' rel='nofollow noopener'>The Dragon Heir</a> The Enchanter Heir, and the Sorcerer Heir. <br/><br/>Chima's</span>
  <span id="freeText2139660312379653065" style="display:none">New York Times bestselling author Cinda Williams Chima comes from a long line of fortune-tellers, musicians and spinners of tales. She began writing romance novels in middle school, which were often confiscated by her teachers.<br /><br />Her Heir Chronicles series (magic comes to contemporary Ohio) comprises <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/213647.The_Warrior_Heir" title="The Warrior Heir" rel="nofollow noopener">The Warrior Heir</a> <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/500743.The_Wizard_Heir" title="The Wizard Heir" rel="nofollow noopener">The Wizard Heir</a> . <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/2866413.The_Dragon_Heir" title="The Dragon Heir" rel="nofollow noopener">The Dragon Heir</a> The Enchanter Heir, and the Sorcerer Heir. <br /><br />Chima's Seven Realms series launched with <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/6342491.The_Demon_King" title="The Demon King" rel="nofollow noopener">The Demon King</a> in 2009; I<a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/7801229.The_Exiled_Queen" title="The Exiled Queen" rel="nofollow noopener">The Exiled Queen</a> in 2010. The Gray Wolf Throne in 2011, and The Crimson Crown (2012.).<br /><br />Her Shattered Realms quartet comprises Flamecaster ( 2016) Shadowcaster (2017) Stormcaster (2018) and Deathcaster scheduled for March 5, 2019. <br /><br />Chima is a graduate of Case Western Reserve University and the University of Akron. Chima has been a workshop leader, panelist, and speaker at writing conferences, including the Northern Ohio SCBWI Conference, the Western Reserve Writers’ Conference, and the World Fantasy Convention. She frequently speaks to young writers and readers at schools and libraries nationwide. <br /><br />Chima lives in Ohio with her family, and is always working on her next novel. </span>
